{
  "content": "# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### What is Server-Side Apply?\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative object management mechanism introduced in Kubernetes 1.18 (GA in 1.22). Unlike the traditional `GET \u2192 modify \u2192 PUT` (or strategic-merge-patch) workflow, SSA moves the merge logic to the server. Each actor\u2014called a **field manager**\u2014declares the fields it intends to own and their desired values. The server maintains a `metadata.managedFields` table that records which manager owns each field. When multiple actors apply to the same object, the server ensures they cannot silently overwrite each other's fields; attempting to set a field already owned by another manager raises an explicit conflict error, unless the request carries `force: true`.\n\n### Where This Lives\n\nThe SSA subsystem spans three packages:\n\n| Package | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Client-side: generated, type-safe patch builders |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Shared: field management middleware (used by both client and server) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | Server-side: HTTP PATCH handler that routes apply requests |\n\nThese three packages form a layered stack, but they have a hard dependency on the external library `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` (SMD, v6), which provides the schema-aware merge algorithm, conflict detection, and fieldpath data structures. **The Kubernetes codebase does not contain the SMD merge algorithm itself**\u2014it only provides the adapters and middleware around it.\n\n### Upstream and Downstream Dependencies\n\n- **Downstream consumers**: Any controller or operator that calls `.Apply(...)` on a typed client from `k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/...` uses this subsystem. So does the `kubectl apply --server-side` command.\n- **Upstream dependencies**: The `managedfields` package requires OpenAPI v3 schema for type-aware merging of built-in resources, and the `k8s.io/kube-openapi/pkg/util/proto` package to parse that schema into the SMD model.\n- **CRD variant**: For Custom Resource Definitions, a separate code path uses a \"deduced\" type converter that treats all map values atomically (no schema-driven list merging).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Generated Apply Configuration Types (`client-go/applyconfigurations/`)\n\nThe `applyconfigurations` package contains code generated by `applyconfiguration-gen`. For every Kubernetes API type (e.g., `apps/v1.Deployment`), there is a parallel mirror struct (e.g., `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`) where **every field is a pointer**. This is the foundational design decision: absent fields produce `omitempty` in JSON/YAML, ensuring only explicitly-stated fields appear in the patch.\n\n```go\n// From staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/meta/v1/objectmeta.go\ntype ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration struct {\n    Name      *string `json:\"name,omitempty\"`\n    Namespace *string `json:\"namespace,omitempty\"`\n    Labels    map[string]string `json:\"labels,omitempty\"`\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nEach field has a `With<FieldName>(value T)` builder method returning a pointer to the receiver, enabling chained calls. This both avoids the awkward `&value` idiom required to set pointer fields and insulates callers from the internal representation.\n\nThe `utils.go` file (generated, 1920 lines) exposes a top-level `ForKind(schema.GroupVersionKind)` function that maps a GVK to its empty apply configuration, enabling dynamic dispatch in generic code.\n\nThe `meta/v1/unstructured.go` file provides `UnstructuredExtractor`, which is discussed in section 4.\n\n**Why a separate type hierarchy is necessary**: the standard Go struct `v1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec` has required (non-pointer) fields like `MaxReplicas`. When marshalled, those zero-valued fields appear in the JSON even when unset, which would direct the autoscaler to downscale to 0. The apply configuration types make every field optional at the Go type level, faithfully expressing \"I have no opinion about this field.\"\n\n### 2.2 The `managedfields` Package and the Manager Stack\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` is the workhorse. The public surface is a single `FieldManager` type (aliased from the internal package) with two methods:\n\n- `Update(liveObj, newObj, manager)` \u2014 for non-apply mutations (PUT, PATCH with other strategies). Records which fields the manager touched.\n- `Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, manager, force)` \u2014 for SSA. Merges the applied configuration onto the live object, detects conflicts, and returns the new merged object plus updated `managedFields`.\n\nInternally, `FieldManager` delegates to a **chain of decorator managers** assembled in `NewDefaultFieldManager`:\n\n```go\n// From staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go\nNewVersionCheckManager(\n  NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n    NewLastAppliedManager(\n      NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n        NewCapManagersManager(\n          NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n            NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n              NewStripMetaManager(f),  // f = structuredMergeManager\n            ), kind.GroupVersion(), subresource,\n          ), DefaultMaxUpdateManagers,  // = 10\n        ), objectCreater, DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability,  // = 1.0\n      ), typeConverter, objectConverter, kind.GroupVersion(),\n    ),\n  ), kind,\n), subresource,\n```\n\nEach decorator in the chain implements the `Manager` interface (`internal/manager.go`):\n\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n    Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, fieldManager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n}\n```\n\nThe innermost manager, `structuredMergeManager`, calls into the SMD library directly.\n\n### 2.3 The HTTP PATCH Handler (`apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`)\n\n`PatchResource` is the HTTP handler factory registered for `PATCH` requests. It reads the `Content-Type` header to determine the patch strategy:\n\n- `application/json-patch+json` \u2192 `jsonPatcher`\n- `application/merge-patch+json` \u2192 `jsonPatcher`\n- `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` \u2192 `smpPatcher`\n- `application/apply-patch+yaml` \u2192 `applyPatcher` \u2190 SSA\n- `application/apply-patch+cbor` \u2192 `applyPatcher` (CBOR variant, gated by feature flag `CBORServingAndStorage`)\n\nOnly the `applyPatcher` invokes `FieldManager.Apply`. The others call `FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors`, which tracks field ownership for non-apply writes but never raises conflict errors.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Client Side\n\nA controller building an SSA request:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/example_test.go:303\ndeploymentApplyConfig := appsv1ac.Deployment(deploymentName, \"default\").\n    WithSpec(appsv1ac.DeploymentSpec().\n        WithReplicas(replicas).\n        WithSelector(metav1ac.LabelSelector().WithMatchLabels(map[string]string{\"app\": \"my-app\"})).\n        WithTemplate(corev1ac.PodTemplateSpec()...),\n    )\n\nresult, err := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Apply(\n    context.TODO(),\n    deploymentApplyConfig,\n    metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"},\n)\n```\n\nInternally the typed client serializes `deploymentApplyConfig` to YAML (only non-nil pointer fields appear) and issues a `PATCH` request with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml` and the query param `fieldManager=my-controller`.\n\n### 3.2 Server-Side: Handler Routing\n\n`PatchResource` (in `patch.go:68`) dispatches to `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject`. This calls:\n\n```go\n// patch.go:514\nobj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n```\n\nThe `fieldManager` here is `scope.FieldManager`, an instance of `*managedfields.FieldManager` pre-built during API server startup via `NewDefaultFieldManager` or `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager`.\n\nFor SSA, `p.forceAllowCreate = true`, meaning if the object does not yet exist in etcd, the apply creates it (via `GuaranteedUpdate`'s create path). The actual store write goes through `p.restPatcher.Update(...)`, which calls `GuaranteedUpdate` on the underlying storage.\n\nThe transform chain is: `applyPatch \u2192 applyAdmission \u2192 dedupOwnerReferences`. Admission runs after the SSA merge, so admission webhooks see the fully-merged object, not just the patch.\n\n### 3.3 Inside `FieldManager.Apply`\n\n```go\n// internal/fieldmanager.go:183\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (object runtime.Object, err error) {\n    managed, err := DecodeManagedFields(accessor.GetManagedFields())\n    object, managed, err = f.fieldManager.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managed, manager, force)\n    if conflicts, ok := err.(merge.Conflicts); ok {\n        return nil, NewConflictError(conflicts)\n    }\n    EncodeObjectManagedFields(object, managed)\n    return object, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe `managed` value is decoded from the live object's `metadata.managedFields` (a JSON-encoded field-set per manager). It is passed through every decorator layer. At the end, `EncodeObjectManagedFields` writes the updated `managedFields` back onto the returned object before it is persisted.\n\n### 3.4 Decorator Execution Order for `Apply`\n\nWhen `Apply` is called, execution flows from the outermost to innermost decorator:\n\n1. **`versionCheckManager`** (`versioncheck.go:47`): Rejects if `appliedObj.GVK != expected GVK`. Prevents accidental cross-version applies.\n\n2. **`lastAppliedUpdater`** (`lastappliedupdater.go`): After the inner chain succeeds, conditionally sets the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation on the live object (only for kubectl applies).\n\n3. **`lastAppliedManager`** (`lastappliedmanager.go:59`): Enables kubectl client-side apply \u2192 server-side apply migration. If the manager is `\"kubectl\"` and there are conflicts, it checks whether each conflicting field is covered by the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation on the live object. Fields in the last-applied annotation are treated as previously \"owned\" by kubectl, so the conflict is silently force-resolved. This allows a seamless upgrade from `kubectl apply` (client-side) to `kubectl apply --server-side` without manual ownership cleanup.\n\n4. **`skipNonAppliedManager`** (`skipnonapplied.go:76`): On the first SSA apply to an object that has never been applied to (empty `managedFields`), it first calls `Update` with the live object against an empty object to create a `\"before-first-apply\"` manager entry for all existing fields. This prevents the first SSA caller from accidentally becoming the owner of all pre-existing fields.\n\n5. **`capManagersManager`** (`capmanagers.go`): After an `Update`, if the number of update-type manager entries exceeds `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers` (10), the oldest entries are merged into a versioned bucket named `\"ancient-changes\"`. This prevents unbounded growth of `managedFields` due to many distinct update managers.\n\n6. **`buildManagerInfoManager`** (`buildmanagerinfo.go`): Stamps each manager entry with a timestamp and API version, building the JSON-encoded manager identifier used as the key in `managedFields`.\n\n7. **`managedFieldsUpdater`** (`managedfieldsupdater.go`): Re-encodes the `Managed` state back into `metadata.managedFields` format on the returned object.\n\n8. **`stripMetaManager`** (`stripmeta.go:36`): Removes a hardcoded set of paths from the manager's tracked field set:\n   - `apiVersion`, `kind`\n   - `metadata`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.namespace`, `metadata.creationTimestamp`, `metadata.selfLink`, `metadata.uid`, `metadata.clusterName`, `metadata.generation`, `metadata.managedFields`, `metadata.resourceVersion`\n\n   These fields are infrastructure fields; tracking them as owned would cause spurious conflicts.\n\n9. **`structuredMergeManager`** (`structuredmerge.go:121`): The terminal manager. Converts the live object and patch object to SMD typed values via `TypeConverter.ObjectToTyped`, then calls `f.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)`. The SMD library computes the merged result and detects conflicts. The merged typed value is converted back to a `runtime.Object` using `TypeConverter.TypedToObject`.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Extract Workflow (Mechanism 2 for Controllers)\n\nWhen a controller cannot safely reconstruct the full desired state on every reconcile (e.g., it has many conditionally-set code paths), it uses the extract-then-apply pattern:\n\n```go\n// From staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go:138\ndeploymentApplyConfig, err := appsv1ac.ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldMgr)\n// modify only what changed\ndeploymentApplyConfig.Spec.Template.Spec.WithContainers(...)\napplied, err := deploymentClient.Apply(ctx, deploymentApplyConfig, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: fieldMgr})\n```\n\n`ExtractDeployment` delegates to `managedfields.ExtractInto`:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go:53\nfunc ExtractInto(object runtime.Object, objectType typed.ParseableType, fieldManager string, applyConfiguration interface{}, subresource string) error {\n    typedObj, _ := toTyped(object, objectType)\n    accessor, _ := meta.Accessor(object)\n    fieldsEntry, ok := findManagedFields(accessor, fieldManager, subresource)\n    // ...\n    fieldset := &fieldpath.Set{}\n    fieldset.FromJSON(bytes.NewReader(fieldsEntry.FieldsV1.Raw))\n    u := typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves()).AsValue().Unstructured()\n    runtime.DefaultUnstructuredConverter.FromUnstructured(u.(map[string]interface{}), applyConfiguration)\n}\n```\n\nThe function:\n1. Finds the `ManagedFieldsEntry` where `Manager == fieldManager` and `Operation == Apply`.\n2. Deserializes the field-set from the `FieldsV1` JSON blob.\n3. Calls `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` to reconstruct only those field paths from the live object.\n4. Converts the result to the typed apply configuration struct.\n\n**Important constraint** (`extract.go:39`): the object passed must be the root resource object, not a subresource. Subresource objects (e.g., `autoscaling.Scale` from `/scale`) do not carry their own `managedFields`. For status, extraction works by passing the root object with `\"status\"` as the subresource parameter, because status fields are at the same field paths in both views.\n\n**For unstructured objects** (dynamic client users), the `UnstructuredExtractor` in `meta/v1/unstructured.go` performs the same logic but returns an `*unstructured.Unstructured`. It fetches the OpenAPI schema via the discovery client, building a `GvkParser` (from `kube-openapi`) that provides a `typed.ParseableType` for the object's GVK. The parser is cached behind a `gvkParserCache` with a 1-minute TTL:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/meta/v1/unstructured.go:33\nconst openAPISchemaTTL = time.Minute\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Conflict Handling\n\n### 5.1 Detection\n\nConflict detection occurs inside the SMD library's `merge.Updater.Apply` call. The library computes the field-set of the incoming patch object, intersects it with the `managedFields` of all other managers, and reports any intersection as a `merge.Conflicts` value (a slice of `merge.Conflict` structs, each containing a manager name and a field path).\n\n### 5.2 Error Representation\n\n`NewConflictError` in `internal/conflict.go` converts `merge.Conflicts` into a `*errors.StatusError` with HTTP status 409 and a `Reason` of `\"Conflict\"`. Each conflicting field becomes a `metav1.StatusCause` of type `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict`, with the `Field` holding the SMD path string and the `Message` identifying the conflicting manager:\n\n```\nApply failed with 2 conflicts:\nconflicts with \"other-controller\":\n- .spec.replicas\nconflicts with \"kube-controller-manager\" using apps/v1 at 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z:\n- .spec.template.spec.containers[name=\"nginx\"].image\n```\n\nThe manager is printed in human-readable form: the JSON-encoded manager key is decoded back into a `ManagedFieldsEntry` struct to extract `Manager`, `Subresource`, `Operation`, `APIVersion`, and `Time`.\n\n### 5.3 Force Resolution\n\nSetting `force: true` in `ApplyOptions` instructs the SMD library to steal ownership of conflicting fields from their current owners. The field manager of the old owner loses those paths in its entry. This is appropriate for controllers that unconditionally own the full desired state of their managed resources. The package documentation (`applyconfigurations/doc.go:112`) explicitly recommends `Force: true` for new controllers.\n\n### 5.4 kubectl Migration Path\n\nThe `lastAppliedManager` layer (`lastappliedmanager.go`) provides a controlled conflict bypass for kubectl. When upgrading from `kubectl apply` (client-side) to `kubectl apply --server-side`, the first SSA apply will conflict because no managed fields were previously tracked. The manager reads the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation, computes what fields it declared, and allows the conflicts for fields that match\u2014without requiring the user to pass `force: true`. Fields not in the annotation still raise errors.\n\nThis logic only triggers when `manager == \"kubectl\"`:\n\n```go\n// lastappliedmanager.go:63\nif manager != \"kubectl\" {\n    return newLiveObj, newManaged, newErr\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Subresource Handling: `ScaleHandler`\n\nThe scale subresource (`/scale`) exposes a different API type (`autoscaling/v1.Scale`) that maps onto fields inside the parent resource (e.g., `spec.replicas` in Deployment). Because the field paths differ between the parent and the subresource view, `ScaleHandler` in `managedfields/scalehandler.go` provides bidirectional translation:\n\n- **`ToSubresource`**: Filters the parent's `managedFields`, keeping only entries that include the resource-specific replicas path, and remaps that path to `spec.replicas` in `autoscaling/v1` terms.\n- **`ToParent`**: Merges scale manager entries back into the parent's `managedFields`, translating the scale path back to the parent's `spec.replicas` path. If the scale manager did not own the replicas path, the parent entry \"steals\" the path back from the scale side.\n\nThis ensures that a controller using `/scale` to change replica counts is correctly attributed ownership of `spec.replicas` in the parent object's `managedFields`.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 7.1 Object Too Large\n\nThe apply patcher does not have a managedFields-stripping fallback for SSA applies. For non-apply patches (JSON, strategic merge), if the object exceeds etcd's size limit after serialization, the server retries after stripping `managedFields` from the object:\n\n```go\n// patch.go:713\nif isTooLargeError(err) && p.patchType != types.ApplyYAMLPatchType && p.patchType != types.ApplyCBORPatchType {\n    // retry without managedFields for non-apply patches\n}\n```\n\nFor SSA applies, no such retry exists. A conflict between object size and the cost of tracking managed fields must be resolved by the operator.\n\n### 7.2 Manager Entry Cap\n\n`DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:35`). When the number of distinct update managers exceeds this, `capManagersManager` merges the oldest into per-version `\"ancient-changes\"` buckets. This loses per-manager granularity. The comment in the source (`capmanagers.go:34`) acknowledges this is a heuristic and the optimal value is uncertain. Notably, **apply managers are not subject to this cap**\u2014only update managers are.\n\n### 7.3 CRD vs. Built-in Resources\n\n`NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` uses `NewCRDStructuredMergeManager`, which injects `newCRDVersionConverter` instead of the standard `newVersionConverter`. CRDs without a schema use `NewDeducedTypeConverter()`, which treats all maps atomically. This means for schemaless CRDs, list merging does not use associative key semantics\u2014the whole list is treated as atomic, and any two managers writing to a list field will conflict.\n\n### 7.4 `managedFields` Must Be Nil in Apply Requests\n\nThe `structuredMergeManager.Apply` method explicitly rejects apply requests that include `metadata.managedFields`:\n\n```go\n// structuredmerge.go:135\nif patchObjMeta.GetManagedFields() != nil {\n    return nil, nil, errors.NewBadRequest(\"metadata.managedFields must be nil\")\n}\n```\n\nThe `applyconfigurations` types do not include a `ManagedFields` field, enforcing this at compile time for typed clients.\n\n### 7.5 Version Mismatch\n\nThe patch object's GVK is validated twice: once by `versionCheckManager` (GVK equality) and once by `structuredMergeManager` (group-version equality against the handler's registered version). Submitting a patch for `apps/v1beta2.Deployment` to an `apps/v1.Deployment` endpoint returns a 400 Bad Request.\n\n### 7.6 Bootstrap Probability\n\n`DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1` means field tracking is started on 100% of object creations. This can be tuned down if the overhead of tracking `managedFields` at creation time is a concern. Setting it to 0 defers tracking until the first SSA apply, using `\"before-first-apply\"` as the synthetic manager for all pre-existing fields.\n\n### 7.7 `managedFields` Cannot Be Directly Reset Except via Sentinel\n\nThe `decodeLiveOrNew` function in `internal/fieldmanager.go` detects an intentional reset if the request object carries `managedFields` set to a non-nil but empty slice (or a slice containing one empty entry). In this case it returns `NewEmptyManaged()`, clearing the field. This is the only sanctioned way to wipe `managedFields` outside of SSA applies.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 8.1 `TypeConverter`\n\nThe `TypeConverter` interface (`managedfields/typeconverter.go`) is the primary extension point:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter = internal.TypeConverter\n```\n\nThree implementations are provided:\n- `NewTypeConverter(openapiSpec, preserveUnknownFields)` \u2014 standard for built-in types with a full OpenAPI schema.\n- `NewDeducedTypeConverter()` \u2014 for CRDs without a schema; all types are atomic.\n- `NewSchemeTypeConverter(scheme, parser)` \u2014 using a runtime `Scheme` and typed parser, primarily for test environments.\n\nA third-party API server can supply a custom `TypeConverter` to integrate SSA with non-OpenAPI schemas.\n\n### 8.2 `resetFields` Filter\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` accepts a `resetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter` argument. This is passed to the SMD `merge.Updater` as `IgnoreFilter`. Fields in this filter are not tracked in `managedFields` at all, regardless of who sets them. This is used for fields that should always be reset by the server (e.g., certain status fields that must not be owned by any client).\n\n### 8.3 Subresource Isolation\n\nThe `FieldManager` is parameterized by `subresource string`. Updates and applies to a subresource endpoint create `ManagedFieldsEntry` items with `Subresource` set, keeping them separate from the main resource's entries. The `findManagedFields` function in `extract.go` matches on both `Manager` and `Subresource`, so the extract workflow correctly handles subresource contexts.\n\n### 8.4 Code Generation\n\nAll apply configuration types are generated by `applyconfiguration-gen` in `k8s.io/code-generator`. Developers adding a new built-in API type must run `hack/update-codegen.sh` to regenerate:\n- The per-type `*ApplyConfiguration` struct.\n- The `With<FieldName>` builder methods.\n- The `Extract<Type>` and `Extract<Type>Status` functions.\n- The `utils.go` dispatch table.\n\nOmitting regeneration causes the typed apply path to fall back to untyped behavior or fail compilation, and means `ExtractInto` cannot reconstruct values for new fields.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Operational Implications\n\n### 9.1 Storage Overhead from `managedFields`\n\nEvery object persisted in etcd carries its `managedFields` as part of the stored JSON. In clusters with many controllers each doing SSA applies, this can be significant. A Deployment managed by three controllers (a Helm controller, a network-policy injector, and a metrics-label stamper) will have three `ManagedFieldsEntry` values in `managedFields`, each containing a serialized fieldpath set. For objects with many fields, these sets can be kilobytes each.\n\nThe cap of 10 update managers (`DefaultMaxUpdateManagers`) helps bound storage growth from non-SSA actors, but **apply managers are not capped**. Each distinct `FieldManager` name used in an SSA apply gets its own entry indefinitely. If a manager name changes (e.g., due to a version suffix rotation), the old entry persists until the object is re-applied by the old manager or the entry is force-applied over.\n\n**Mitigation**: Operators should name their field managers consistently (one name per reconciliation loop), avoid unnecessary field changes, and prefer `Force: true` in controllers that fully own their fields to prevent orphaned ownership entries. Periodically re-applying with the same manager name updates the timestamp and field set, superseding old entries.\n\n### 9.2 OpenAPI Schema Caching for Extraction\n\nThe `UnstructuredExtractor` caches the parsed OpenAPI schema for 1 minute (`openAPISchemaTTL`). During this window, a newly-added CRD field will not be extractable. The cache is per-extractor instance; callers should reuse a single extractor rather than creating one per request.\n\n### 9.3 Conflict Retries and Controller Overhead\n\nControllers using SSA with `Force: false` may experience conflict errors when another controller concurrently manages overlapping fields. This forces a retry loop. Each retry requires a GET (or informer read) and a PATCH. At scale, this increases API server load. Best practice is to design controllers so field ownership is non-overlapping. `Force: true` is appropriate for controllers that are the sole authority over a well-defined set of fields.\n\n### 9.4 Apply as Create\n\nBecause `forceAllowCreate = true` is set for apply requests (`patch.go:674`), an SSA apply to a non-existent object creates it. The `GuaranteedUpdate` call hits the storage `Create` path. This can cause surprising behavior: an apply with `Force: false` against a non-existent resource will succeed (create), even though force semantics only matter for conflict resolution on existing objects.\n\n### 9.5 Admission Webhook Interaction\n\nMutating admission webhooks run after the SSA merge but before the object is written to storage. This means a mutating webhook can add or change fields in the merged result. Those changes are attributed to the server (not to any SSA manager), so they will not appear in any manager's field set unless the manager explicitly includes them in a subsequent apply. This can cause repeated webhook-vs-apply churn if a webhook continuously sets a field that an SSA controller omits.\n\n### 9.6 Debugging `managedFields`\n\nThe `managedFields` table is visible on every `kubectl get` with `-o json` or `-o yaml`. Each entry contains:\n- `manager`: the field manager name\n- `operation`: `Apply` or `Update`\n- `apiVersion`: the version the manager last applied/updated in\n- `time`: timestamp of last operation\n- `fieldsV1`: a compact JSON representation of the owned field paths\n\nThe `fieldsV1` encoding uses a nested map structure where keys are field names prefixed with `f:` for struct fields and `k:` for associative list keys. The SMD library provides tooling to decode these for debugging.\n\n---\n\n## 10. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Root of all generated apply configuration types |\n| {
  "content": "# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations: A Deep Guide\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### What is Server-Side Apply?\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative object management mechanism introduced in Kubernetes 1.18 (GA in 1.22). Unlike the traditional `GET \u2192 modify \u2192 PUT` (or strategic-merge-patch) workflow, SSA moves the merge logic to the server. Each actor\u2014called a **field manager**\u2014declares the fields it intends to own and their desired values. The server maintains a `metadata.managedFields` table that records which manager owns each field. When multiple actors apply to the same object, the server ensures they cannot silently overwrite each other's fields; attempting to set a field already owned by another manager raises an explicit conflict error, unless the request carries `force: true`.\n\n### Where This Lives\n\nThe SSA subsystem spans three packages:\n\n| Package | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Client-side: generated, type-safe patch builders |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Shared: field management middleware (used by both client and server) |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | Server-side: HTTP PATCH handler that routes apply requests |\n\nThese three packages form a layered stack, but they have a hard dependency on the external library `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` (SMD, v6), which provides the schema-aware merge algorithm, conflict detection, and fieldpath data structures. **The Kubernetes codebase does not contain the SMD merge algorithm itself**\u2014it only provides the adapters and middleware around it.\n\n### Upstream and Downstream Dependencies\n\n- **Downstream consumers**: Any controller or operator that calls `.Apply(...)` on a typed client from `k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes/typed/...` uses this subsystem. So does the `kubectl apply --server-side` command.\n- **Upstream dependencies**: The `managedfields` package requires OpenAPI v3 schema for type-aware merging of built-in resources, and the `k8s.io/kube-openapi/pkg/util/proto` package to parse that schema into the SMD model.\n- **CRD variant**: For Custom Resource Definitions, a separate code path uses a \"deduced\" type converter that treats all map values atomically (no schema-driven list merging).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Generated Apply Configuration Types (`client-go/applyconfigurations/`)\n\nThe `applyconfigurations` package contains code generated by `applyconfiguration-gen`. For every Kubernetes API type (e.g., `apps/v1.Deployment`), there is a parallel mirror struct (e.g., `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`) where **every field is a pointer**. This is the foundational design decision: absent fields produce `omitempty` in JSON/YAML, ensuring only explicitly-stated fields appear in the patch.\n\n```go\n// From staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/meta/v1/objectmeta.go\ntype ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration struct {\n    Name      *string `json:\"name,omitempty\"`\n    Namespace *string `json:\"namespace,omitempty\"`\n    Labels    map[string]string `json:\"labels,omitempty\"`\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nEach field has a `With<FieldName>(value T)` builder method returning a pointer to the receiver, enabling chained calls. This both avoids the awkward `&value` idiom required to set pointer fields and insulates callers from the internal representation.\n\nThe `utils.go` file (generated, 1920 lines) exposes a top-level `ForKind(schema.GroupVersionKind)` function that maps a GVK to its empty apply configuration, enabling dynamic dispatch in generic code.\n\nThe `meta/v1/unstructured.go` file provides `UnstructuredExtractor`, which is discussed in section 4.\n\n**Why a separate type hierarchy is necessary**: the standard Go struct `v1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec` has required (non-pointer) fields like `MaxReplicas`. When marshalled, those zero-valued fields appear in the JSON even when unset, which would direct the autoscaler to downscale to 0. The apply configuration types make every field optional at the Go type level, faithfully expressing \"I have no opinion about this field.\"\n\n### 2.2 The `managedfields` Package and the Manager Stack\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` is the workhorse. The public surface is a single `FieldManager` type (aliased from the internal package) with two methods:\n\n- `Update(liveObj, newObj, manager)` \u2014 for non-apply mutations (PUT, PATCH with other strategies). Records which fields the manager touched.\n- `Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, manager, force)` \u2014 for SSA. Merges the applied configuration onto the live object, detects conflicts, and returns the new merged object plus updated `managedFields`.\n\nInternally, `FieldManager` delegates to a **chain of decorator managers** assembled in `NewDefaultFieldManager`:\n\n```go\n// From staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go\nNewVersionCheckManager(\n  NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n    NewLastAppliedManager(\n      NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n        NewCapManagersManager(\n          NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n            NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n              NewStripMetaManager(f),  // f = structuredMergeManager\n            ), kind.GroupVersion(), subresource,\n          ), DefaultMaxUpdateManagers,  // = 10\n        ), objectCreater, DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability,  // = 1.0\n      ), typeConverter, objectConverter, kind.GroupVersion(),\n    ),\n  ), kind,\n), subresource,\n```\n\nEach decorator in the chain implements the `Manager` interface (`internal/manager.go`):\n\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n    Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, fieldManager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n}\n```\n\nThe innermost manager, `structuredMergeManager`, calls into the SMD library directly.\n\n### 2.3 The HTTP PATCH Handler (`apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`)\n\n`PatchResource` is the HTTP handler factory registered for `PATCH` requests. It reads the `Content-Type` header to determine the patch strategy:\n\n- `application/json-patch+json` \u2192 `jsonPatcher`\n- `application/merge-patch+json` \u2192 `jsonPatcher`\n- `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` \u2192 `smpPatcher`\n- `application/apply-patch+yaml` \u2192 `applyPatcher` \u2190 SSA\n- `application/apply-patch+cbor` \u2192 `applyPatcher` (CBOR variant, gated by feature flag `CBORServingAndStorage`)\n\nOnly the `applyPatcher` invokes `FieldManager.Apply`. The others call `FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors`, which tracks field ownership for non-apply writes but never raises conflict errors.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Client Side\n\nA controller building an SSA request:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/example_test.go:303\ndeploymentApplyConfig := appsv1ac.Deployment(deploymentName, \"default\").\n    WithSpec(appsv1ac.DeploymentSpec().\n        WithReplicas(replicas).\n        WithSelector(metav1ac.LabelSelector().WithMatchLabels(map[string]string{\"app\": \"my-app\"})).\n        WithTemplate(corev1ac.PodTemplateSpec()...),\n    )\n\nresult, err := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Apply(\n    context.TODO(),\n    deploymentApplyConfig,\n    metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"},\n)\n```\n\nInternally the typed client serializes `deploymentApplyConfig` to YAML (only non-nil pointer fields appear) and issues a `PATCH` request with `Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml` and the query param `fieldManager=my-controller`.\n\n### 3.2 Server-Side: Handler Routing\n\n`PatchResource` (in `patch.go:68`) dispatches to `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject`. This calls:\n\n```go\n// patch.go:514\nobj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n```\n\nThe `fieldManager` here is `scope.FieldManager`, an instance of `*managedfields.FieldManager` pre-built during API server startup via `NewDefaultFieldManager` or `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager`.\n\nFor SSA, `p.forceAllowCreate = true`, meaning if the object does not yet exist in etcd, the apply creates it (via `GuaranteedUpdate`'s create path). The actual store write goes through `p.restPatcher.Update(...)`, which calls `GuaranteedUpdate` on the underlying storage.\n\nThe transform chain is: `applyPatch \u2192 applyAdmission \u2192 dedupOwnerReferences`. Admission runs after the SSA merge, so admission webhooks see the fully-merged object, not just the patch.\n\n### 3.3 Inside `FieldManager.Apply`\n\n```go\n// internal/fieldmanager.go:183\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (object runtime.Object, err error) {\n    managed, err := DecodeManagedFields(accessor.GetManagedFields())\n    object, managed, err = f.fieldManager.Apply(liveObj, appliedObj, managed, manager, force)\n    if conflicts, ok := err.(merge.Conflicts); ok {\n        return nil, NewConflictError(conflicts)\n    }\n    EncodeObjectManagedFields(object, managed)\n    return object, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe `managed` value is decoded from the live object's `metadata.managedFields` (a JSON-encoded field-set per manager). It is passed through every decorator layer. At the end, `EncodeObjectManagedFields` writes the updated `managedFields` back onto the returned object before it is persisted.\n\n### 3.4 Decorator Execution Order for `Apply`\n\nWhen `Apply` is called, execution flows from the outermost to innermost decorator:\n\n1. **`versionCheckManager`** (`versioncheck.go:47`): Rejects if `appliedObj.GVK != expected GVK`. Prevents accidental cross-version applies.\n\n2. **`lastAppliedUpdater`** (`lastappliedupdater.go`): After the inner chain succeeds, conditionally sets the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation on the live object (only for kubectl applies).\n\n3. **`lastAppliedManager`** (`lastappliedmanager.go:59`): Enables kubectl client-side apply \u2192 server-side apply migration. If the manager is `\"kubectl\"` and there are conflicts, it checks whether each conflicting field is covered by the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation on the live object. Fields in the last-applied annotation are treated as previously \"owned\" by kubectl, so the conflict is silently force-resolved. This allows a seamless upgrade from `kubectl apply` (client-side) to `kubectl apply --server-side` without manual ownership cleanup.\n\n4. **`skipNonAppliedManager`** (`skipnonapplied.go:76`): On the first SSA apply to an object that has never been applied to (empty `managedFields`), it first calls `Update` with the live object against an empty object to create a `\"before-first-apply\"` manager entry for all existing fields. This prevents the first SSA caller from accidentally becoming the owner of all pre-existing fields.\n\n5. **`capManagersManager`** (`capmanagers.go`): After an `Update`, if the number of update-type manager entries exceeds `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers` (10), the oldest entries are merged into a versioned bucket named `\"ancient-changes\"`. This prevents unbounded growth of `managedFields` due to many distinct update managers.\n\n6. **`buildManagerInfoManager`** (`buildmanagerinfo.go`): Stamps each manager entry with a timestamp and API version, building the JSON-encoded manager identifier used as the key in `managedFields`.\n\n7. **`managedFieldsUpdater`** (`managedfieldsupdater.go`): Re-encodes the `Managed` state back into `metadata.managedFields` format on the returned object.\n\n8. **`stripMetaManager`** (`stripmeta.go:36`): Removes a hardcoded set of paths from the manager's tracked field set:\n   - `apiVersion`, `kind`\n   - `metadata`, `metadata.name`, `metadata.namespace`, `metadata.creationTimestamp`, `metadata.selfLink`, `metadata.uid`, `metadata.clusterName`, `metadata.generation`, `metadata.managedFields`, `metadata.resourceVersion`\n\n   These fields are infrastructure fields; tracking them as owned would cause spurious conflicts.\n\n9. **`structuredMergeManager`** (`structuredmerge.go:121`): The terminal manager. Converts the live object and patch object to SMD typed values via `TypeConverter.ObjectToTyped`, then calls `f.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)`. The SMD library computes the merged result and detects conflicts. The merged typed value is converted back to a `runtime.Object` using `TypeConverter.TypedToObject`.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Extract Workflow (Mechanism 2 for Controllers)\n\nWhen a controller cannot safely reconstruct the full desired state on every reconcile (e.g., it has many conditionally-set code paths), it uses the extract-then-apply pattern:\n\n```go\n// From staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go:138\ndeploymentApplyConfig, err := appsv1ac.ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldMgr)\n// modify only what changed\ndeploymentApplyConfig.Spec.Template.Spec.WithContainers(...)\napplied, err := deploymentClient.Apply(ctx, deploymentApplyConfig, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: fieldMgr})\n```\n\n`ExtractDeployment` delegates to `managedfields.ExtractInto`:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go:53\nfunc ExtractInto(object runtime.Object, objectType typed.ParseableType, fieldManager string, applyConfiguration interface{}, subresource string) error {\n    typedObj, _ := toTyped(object, objectType)\n    accessor, _ := meta.Accessor(object)\n    fieldsEntry, ok := findManagedFields(accessor, fieldManager, subresource)\n    // ...\n    fieldset := &fieldpath.Set{}\n    fieldset.FromJSON(bytes.NewReader(fieldsEntry.FieldsV1.Raw))\n    u := typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves()).AsValue().Unstructured()\n    runtime.DefaultUnstructuredConverter.FromUnstructured(u.(map[string]interface{}), applyConfiguration)\n}\n```\n\nThe function:\n1. Finds the `ManagedFieldsEntry` where `Manager == fieldManager` and `Operation == Apply`.\n2. Deserializes the field-set from the `FieldsV1` JSON blob.\n3. Calls `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` to reconstruct only those field paths from the live object.\n4. Converts the result to the typed apply configuration struct.\n\n**Important constraint** (`extract.go:39`): the object passed must be the root resource object, not a subresource. Subresource objects (e.g., `autoscaling.Scale` from `/scale`) do not carry their own `managedFields`. For status, extraction works by passing the root object with `\"status\"` as the subresource parameter, because status fields are at the same field paths in both views.\n\n**For unstructured objects** (dynamic client users), the `UnstructuredExtractor` in `meta/v1/unstructured.go` performs the same logic but returns an `*unstructured.Unstructured`. It fetches the OpenAPI schema via the discovery client, building a `GvkParser` (from `kube-openapi`) that provides a `typed.ParseableType` for the object's GVK. The parser is cached behind a `gvkParserCache` with a 1-minute TTL:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/meta/v1/unstructured.go:33\nconst openAPISchemaTTL = time.Minute\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Conflict Handling\n\n### 5.1 Detection\n\nConflict detection occurs inside the SMD library's `merge.Updater.Apply` call. The library computes the field-set of the incoming patch object, intersects it with the `managedFields` of all other managers, and reports any intersection as a `merge.Conflicts` value (a slice of `merge.Conflict` structs, each containing a manager name and a field path).\n\n### 5.2 Error Representation\n\n`NewConflictError` in `internal/conflict.go` converts `merge.Conflicts` into a `*errors.StatusError` with HTTP status 409 and a `Reason` of `\"Conflict\"`. Each conflicting field becomes a `metav1.StatusCause` of type `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict`, with the `Field` holding the SMD path string and the `Message` identifying the conflicting manager:\n\n```\nApply failed with 2 conflicts:\nconflicts with \"other-controller\":\n- .spec.replicas\nconflicts with \"kube-controller-manager\" using apps/v1 at 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z:\n- .spec.template.spec.containers[name=\"nginx\"].image\n```\n\nThe manager is printed in human-readable form: the JSON-encoded manager key is decoded back into a `ManagedFieldsEntry` struct to extract `Manager`, `Subresource`, `Operation`, `APIVersion`, and `Time`.\n\n### 5.3 Force Resolution\n\nSetting `force: true` in `ApplyOptions` instructs the SMD library to steal ownership of conflicting fields from their current owners. The field manager of the old owner loses those paths in its entry. This is appropriate for controllers that unconditionally own the full desired state of their managed resources. The package documentation (`applyconfigurations/doc.go:112`) explicitly recommends `Force: true` for new controllers.\n\n### 5.4 kubectl Migration Path\n\nThe `lastAppliedManager` layer (`lastappliedmanager.go`) provides a controlled conflict bypass for kubectl. When upgrading from `kubectl apply` (client-side) to `kubectl apply --server-side`, the first SSA apply will conflict because no managed fields were previously tracked. The manager reads the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation, computes what fields it declared, and allows the conflicts for fields that match\u2014without requiring the user to pass `force: true`. Fields not in the annotation still raise errors.\n\nThis logic only triggers when `manager == \"kubectl\"`:\n\n```go\n// lastappliedmanager.go:63\nif manager != \"kubectl\" {\n    return newLiveObj, newManaged, newErr\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Subresource Handling: `ScaleHandler`\n\nThe scale subresource (`/scale`) exposes a different API type (`autoscaling/v1.Scale`) that maps onto fields inside the parent resource (e.g., `spec.replicas` in Deployment). Because the field paths differ between the parent and the subresource view, `ScaleHandler` in `managedfields/scalehandler.go` provides bidirectional translation:\n\n- **`ToSubresource`**: Filters the parent's `managedFields`, keeping only entries that include the resource-specific replicas path, and remaps that path to `spec.replicas` in `autoscaling/v1` terms.\n- **`ToParent`**: Merges scale manager entries back into the parent's `managedFields`, translating the scale path back to the parent's `spec.replicas` path. If the scale manager did not own the replicas path, the parent entry \"steals\" the path back from the scale side.\n\nThis ensures that a controller using `/scale` to change replica counts is correctly attributed ownership of `spec.replicas` in the parent object's `managedFields`.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 7.1 Object Too Large\n\nThe apply patcher does not have a managedFields-stripping fallback for SSA applies. For non-apply patches (JSON, strategic merge), if the object exceeds etcd's size limit after serialization, the server retries after stripping `managedFields` from the object:\n\n```go\n// patch.go:713\nif isTooLargeError(err) && p.patchType != types.ApplyYAMLPatchType && p.patchType != types.ApplyCBORPatchType {\n    // retry without managedFields for non-apply patches\n}\n```\n\nFor SSA applies, no such retry exists. A conflict between object size and the cost of tracking managed fields must be resolved by the operator.\n\n### 7.2 Manager Entry Cap\n\n`DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10` (`internal/fieldmanager.go:35`). When the number of distinct update managers exceeds this, `capManagersManager` merges the oldest into per-version `\"ancient-changes\"` buckets. This loses per-manager granularity. The comment in the source (`capmanagers.go:34`) acknowledges this is a heuristic and the optimal value is uncertain. Notably, **apply managers are not subject to this cap**\u2014only update managers are.\n\n### 7.3 CRD vs. Built-in Resources\n\n`NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` uses `NewCRDStructuredMergeManager`, which injects `newCRDVersionConverter` instead of the standard `newVersionConverter`. CRDs without a schema use `NewDeducedTypeConverter()`, which treats all maps atomically. This means for schemaless CRDs, list merging does not use associative key semantics\u2014the whole list is treated as atomic, and any two managers writing to a list field will conflict.\n\n### 7.4 `managedFields` Must Be Nil in Apply Requests\n\nThe `structuredMergeManager.Apply` method explicitly rejects apply requests that include `metadata.managedFields`:\n\n```go\n// structuredmerge.go:135\nif patchObjMeta.GetManagedFields() != nil {\n    return nil, nil, errors.NewBadRequest(\"metadata.managedFields must be nil\")\n}\n```\n\nThe `applyconfigurations` types do not include a `ManagedFields` field, enforcing this at compile time for typed clients.\n\n### 7.5 Version Mismatch\n\nThe patch object's GVK is validated twice: once by `versionCheckManager` (GVK equality) and once by `structuredMergeManager` (group-version equality against the handler's registered version). Submitting a patch for `apps/v1beta2.Deployment` to an `apps/v1.Deployment` endpoint returns a 400 Bad Request.\n\n### 7.6 Bootstrap Probability\n\n`DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1` means field tracking is started on 100% of object creations. This can be tuned down if the overhead of tracking `managedFields` at creation time is a concern. Setting it to 0 defers tracking until the first SSA apply, using `\"before-first-apply\"` as the synthetic manager for all pre-existing fields.\n\n### 7.7 `managedFields` Cannot Be Directly Reset Except via Sentinel\n\nThe `decodeLiveOrNew` function in `internal/fieldmanager.go` detects an intentional reset if the request object carries `managedFields` set to a non-nil but empty slice (or a slice containing one empty entry). In this case it returns `NewEmptyManaged()`, clearing the field. This is the only sanctioned way to wipe `managedFields` outside of SSA applies.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 8.1 `TypeConverter`\n\nThe `TypeConverter` interface (`managedfields/typeconverter.go`) is the primary extension point:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter = internal.TypeConverter\n```\n\nThree implementations are provided:\n- `NewTypeConverter(openapiSpec, preserveUnknownFields)` \u2014 standard for built-in types with a full OpenAPI schema.\n- `NewDeducedTypeConverter()` \u2014 for CRDs without a schema; all types are atomic.\n- `NewSchemeTypeConverter(scheme, parser)` \u2014 using a runtime `Scheme` and typed parser, primarily for test environments.\n\nA third-party API server can supply a custom `TypeConverter` to integrate SSA with non-OpenAPI schemas.\n\n### 8.2 `resetFields` Filter\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` accepts a `resetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter` argument. This is passed to the SMD `merge.Updater` as `IgnoreFilter`. Fields in this filter are not tracked in `managedFields` at all, regardless of who sets them. This is used for fields that should always be reset by the server (e.g., certain status fields that must not be owned by any client).\n\n### 8.3 Subresource Isolation\n\nThe `FieldManager` is parameterized by `subresource string`. Updates and applies to a subresource endpoint create `ManagedFieldsEntry` items with `Subresource` set, keeping them separate from the main resource's entries. The `findManagedFields` function in `extract.go` matches on both `Manager` and `Subresource`, so the extract workflow correctly handles subresource contexts.\n\n### 8.4 Code Generation\n\nAll apply configuration types are generated by `applyconfiguration-gen` in `k8s.io/code-generator`. Developers adding a new built-in API type must run `hack/update-codegen.sh` to regenerate:\n- The per-type `*ApplyConfiguration` struct.\n- The `With<FieldName>` builder methods.\n- The `Extract<Type>` and `Extract<Type>Status` functions.\n- The `utils.go` dispatch table.\n\nOmitting regeneration causes the typed apply path to fall back to untyped behavior or fail compilation, and means `ExtractInto` cannot reconstruct values for new fields.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Operational Implications\n\n### 9.1 Storage Overhead from `managedFields`\n\nEvery object persisted in etcd carries its `managedFields` as part of the stored JSON. In clusters with many controllers each doing SSA applies, this can be significant. A Deployment managed by three controllers (a Helm controller, a network-policy injector, and a metrics-label stamper) will have three `ManagedFieldsEntry` values in `managedFields`, each containing a serialized fieldpath set. For objects with many fields, these sets can be kilobytes each.\n\nThe cap of 10 update managers (`DefaultMaxUpdateManagers`) helps bound storage growth from non-SSA actors, but **apply managers are not capped**. Each distinct `FieldManager` name used in an SSA apply gets its own entry indefinitely. If a manager name changes (e.g., due to a version suffix rotation), the old entry persists until the object is re-applied by the old manager or the entry is force-applied over.\n\n**Mitigation**: Operators should name their field managers consistently (one name per reconciliation loop), avoid unnecessary field changes, and prefer `Force: true` in controllers that fully own their fields to prevent orphaned ownership entries. Periodically re-applying with the same manager name updates the timestamp and field set, superseding old entries.\n\n### 9.2 OpenAPI Schema Caching for Extraction\n\nThe `UnstructuredExtractor` caches the parsed OpenAPI schema for 1 minute (`openAPISchemaTTL`). During this window, a newly-added CRD field will not be extractable. The cache is per-extractor instance; callers should reuse a single extractor rather than creating one per request.\n\n### 9.3 Conflict Retries and Controller Overhead\n\nControllers using SSA with `Force: false` may experience conflict errors when another controller concurrently manages overlapping fields. This forces a retry loop. Each retry requires a GET (or informer read) and a PATCH. At scale, this increases API server load. Best practice is to design controllers so field ownership is non-overlapping. `Force: true` is appropriate for controllers that are the sole authority over a well-defined set of fields.\n\n### 9.4 Apply as Create\n\nBecause `forceAllowCreate = true` is set for apply requests (`patch.go:674`), an SSA apply to a non-existent object creates it. The `GuaranteedUpdate` call hits the storage `Create` path. This can cause surprising behavior: an apply with `Force: false` against a non-existent resource will succeed (create), even though force semantics only matter for conflict resolution on existing objects.\n\n### 9.5 Admission Webhook Interaction\n\nMutating admission webhooks run after the SSA merge but before the object is written to storage. This means a mutating webhook can add or change fields in the merged result. Those changes are attributed to the server (not to any SSA manager), so they will not appear in any manager's field set unless the manager explicitly includes them in a subsequent apply. This can cause repeated webhook-vs-apply churn if a webhook continuously sets a field that an SSA controller omits.\n\n### 9.6 Debugging `managedFields`\n\nThe `managedFields` table is visible on every `kubectl get` with `-o json` or `-o yaml`. Each entry contains:\n- `manager`: the field manager name\n- `operation`: `Apply` or `Update`\n- `apiVersion`: the version the manager last applied/updated in\n- `time`: timestamp of last operation\n- `fieldsV1`: a compact JSON representation of the owned field paths\n\nThe `fieldsV1` encoding uses a nested map structure where keys are field names prefixed with `f:` for struct fields and `k:` for associative list keys. The SMD library provides tooling to decode these for debugging.\n\n---\n\n## 10. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Root of all generated apply configuration types |\n| # Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations: A Deep Guide

---

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

### What is Server-Side Apply?

Server-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative object management mechanism introduced in Kubernetes 1.18 (GA in 1.22). Unlike the traditional `GET → modify → PUT` (or strategic-merge-patch) workflow, SSA moves the merge logic to the server. Each actor—called a **field manager**—declares the fields it intends to own and their desired values. The server maintains a `metadata.managedFields` table that records which manager owns each field. When multiple actors apply to the same object, the server ensures they cannot silently overwrite each other's fields; attempting to set a field already owned by another manager raises an explicit conflict error, unless the request carries `force: true`.

### Where This Lives

The SSA subsystem spans three packages:

| Package | Role |
|---|---|
| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Client-side: generated, type-safe patch builders |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Shared: field management middleware (used by both client and server) |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | Server-side: HTTP PATCH handler that routes apply requests |

These three packages form a layered stack, but they have a hard dependency on the external library `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` (SMD, v6), which provides the schema-aware merge algorithm, conflict detection, and fieldpath data structures. **The Kubernetes codebase does not contain the SMD merge algorithm itself**—it only provides the adapters and middleware around it.

### Upstream and Downstream Dependencies

- **Downstream consumers**: Any controller or operator that calls 
... (truncated)

# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and applyconfigurations: A Deep Guide

---

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

### What is Server-Side Apply?

Server-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative object management mechanism introduced in Kubernetes 1.18 (GA in 1.22). Unlike the traditional `GET → modify → PUT` (or strategic-merge-patch) workflow, SSA moves the merge logic to the server. Each actor—called a **field manager**—declares the fields it intends to own and their desired values. The server maintains a `metadata.managedFields` table that records which manager owns each field. When multiple actors apply to the same object, the server ensures they cannot silently overwrite each other's fields; attempting to set a field already owned by another manager raises an explicit conflict error, unless the request carries `force: true`.

### Where This Lives

The SSA subsystem spans three packages:

| Package | Role |
|---|---|
| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Client-side: generated, type-safe patch builders |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/` | Shared: field management middleware (used by both client and server) |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | Server-side: HTTP PATCH handler that routes apply requests |

These three packages form a layered stack, but they have a hard dependency on the external library `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` (SMD, v6), which provides the schema-aware merge algorithm, conflict detection, and fieldpath data structures. **The Kubernetes codebase does not contain the SMD merge algorithm itself**—it only provides the adapters and middleware around it.

- **Downstream consumers**: Any controller or operator that calls
